[7351.92 --> 7356.10]  freezing and other performance hiccups that have plagued high-end Asus laptops
[7356.10 --> 7357.12]  since 2021.
[7357.62 --> 7361.90]  For years, users have reported stuttering during basic tasks like YouTube playback,
[7362.28 --> 7364.56]  audio crackles and pops on Discord calls,

[7368.60 --> 7372.76]  The problems impact millions of Asus Strix, Scar and Zephyrus laptops,
[7372.76 --> 7378.18]  which typically include top-tier Intel CPUs, RTX 30 or 40 series GPUs,
[7378.48 --> 7379.38]  and plenty of RAM.
[7379.72 --> 7382.52]  Users typically report trying everything to fix their systems,
[7382.52 --> 7384.34]  with many even installing Linux,
[7384.56 --> 7387.86]  only to find the problems persist regardless of the operating system.
[7387.96 --> 7388.62]  Which is pretty wild.

[7392.08 --> 7396.10]  where the system just, the main screen just stops working randomly,
[7396.20 --> 7397.44]  and I have to close it and open it again.
[7397.50 --> 7398.04]  It's fantastic.
[7400.04 --> 7402.02]  Using freely available tools,
[7402.36 --> 7405.86]  Zefkek was able to monitor process latencies under Windows

[7408.06 --> 7411.06]  finding enough evidence to implicate high DPC,
[7411.40 --> 7412.80]  or deferred procedure call,
[7413.12 --> 7416.22]  latency originating with ACPI.Sys.
[7416.70 --> 7419.80]  But that doesn't mean it's a Windows problem.
[7420.14 --> 7422.70]  ACPI.Sys isn't a typical driver.
[7422.92 --> 7426.76]  It's effectively an interpreter for the ACPI machine language,
[7427.30 --> 7430.44]  the code provided by the laptop's firmware.
[7430.44 --> 7433.02]  If ACPI.Sys is slow,
[7433.34 --> 7437.06]  it's because the firmware is passing inefficient or flawed code to execute.
[7437.60 --> 7438.22]  Not good.
[7438.52 --> 7439.14]  Digging further,

[7442.70 --> 7446.26]  They recur reliably every 30 to 60 seconds.
[7446.58 --> 7450.00]  While random interruptions might point to thermal throttling,
[7450.26 --> 7452.82]  a repeating pattern shows that it's a systemic issue,
[7452.94 --> 7455.94]  perhaps a timer or a scheduled event in the system logic.
[7456.44 --> 7457.98]  Reviewing raw event data,

[7470.18 --> 7474.16]  Reviewing raw event data uncovered a high priority interrupt handler,
[7474.88 --> 7476.68]  GPE-LO2,

[7480.50 --> 7482.92]  which, as far as high priority interrupts go,
